The central question that usefulness checking answers is:\n10: \"in this match expression, is that branch redundant?\".\n11: More precisely, it boils down to computing whether,\n12: given a list of patterns we have already seen,\n13: a given new pattern might match any new value.\n14: \n15: For example, in the following match expression,\n16: we ask in turn whether each pattern might match something\n17: that wasn't matched by the patterns above it.\n18: Here we see the 4th pattern is redundant with the 1st;\n19: that branch will get an \"unreachable\" warning.\n20: The 3rd pattern may Analysis\n\n### Strategy\n\nThis refactoring affects the core type system of the Rust compiler across multiple crates:\n\n1. **rustc_type_ir** - Contains the generic definition and trait bounds\n2. **rustc_middle** - Contains type aliases for the tcx-specific version\n3. **rustc_public** - Contains the public FFI definition\n4. **rustc_infer** - Uses it in type inference\n5. **rustc_hir_typeck** **rust-analyzer** - Has its own versions of the types\n\n### Key Considerations\n\n1. **Field semantics**: The field rename from `a`/`b` to `sub_ty`/`super_ty` makes the semantics clear - `sub_ty` is the subtype and `super_ty` is the supertype in the subtype relation `sub_ty <: super_ty`.\n\n2. **Breaking changes**: This is a breaking change to the internal API. All code that pattern-matches on `SubtypePredicate` or constructs it must be updated.\n\n3. **Preservation of logic**: The refactoring is purely a renaming - no logic changes are required. All field access must be updated to use the new names.\n\n4. **Compilation order**: Changes must be made in dependency order:\n   - Start with the definitions (rustc_type_ir, rustc_public)\n   - Then type aliases and re-exports\n   - Then trait bounds and type system\n   - Finally all usage sites\n\n### Verification\n\nTo verify the refactoring is complete:\n\n1. the subtype and `super_ty` is the supertype in the subtype relation `sub_ty <: super_ty`.\n\n2. **Breaking changes**: This is a breaking change to the internal API. All code that pattern-matches on `SubtypePredicate` or constructs it must be updated.\n\n3. **Preservation of logic**: The refactoring is purely a renaming - no logic changes are required. 733→\n   734→## Analysis\n   735→\n   736→### Strategy\n   737→\n   738→This refactoring affects the core type system of the Rust compiler across multiple crates:\n   739→\n   740→1. **rustc_type_ir** - Contains the generic definition and trait bounds\n   741→2. **rustc_middle** - Contains type aliases for the tcx-specific version\n   742→3. **rustc_public** - Contains the public FFI definition\n   743→4. **rustc_infer** - Uses it in type inference\n   744→5. **rustc_hir_typeck** - Uses it in fallback type inference\n   745→6. **rustc_trait_selection** - Uses it in obligation fulfillment and error reporting\n   746→7. **rustc_next_trait_solver** - Uses it in the next-gen trait solver\n   747→8. **rust-analyzer** - Has its own versions of the types\n   748→\n   749→### Key Considerations\n   750→\n   751→1. **Field semantics**: The field rename from `a`/`b` to `sub_ty`/`super_ty` makes the semantics clear - `sub_ty` is the subtype and `super_ty` is the supertype in the subtype relation `sub_ty <: super_ty`.\n   752→\n   753→2. **Breaking changes**: This is a breaking change to the internal API. TyKind::RigidTy(RigidTy::Adt(def, _)) => def.is_box(),\n            _ => false,\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn is_simd(&self) -> bool {\n        matches!(self, TyKind::RigidTy(RigidTy::Adt(def, _)) if def.is_simd())\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_principal(&self) -> Option<Binder<ExistentialTraitRef>> {\n        if let TyKind::RigidTy(RigidTy::Dynamic(predicates, _)) = self {\n            if let Some(Binder { value: ExistentialPredicate::Trait(trait_ref), bound_vars }) =\n                predicates.first()\n            {\n                Some(Binder { value: trait_ref.clone(), bound_vars: bound_vars.clone() })\n            } else {\n                None\n            }\n        } else {\n            None\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the type of `ty[i]` for builtin types.\n    pub fn builtin_index(&self) -> Option<Ty> {\n        match self.rigid()? {\n            RigidTy::Array(ty, _) | RigidTy::Slice(ty) => Some(*ty),\n            _ => None,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the type and mutability of `*ty` for builtin types.\n    ///\n    /// The parameter `explicit` indicates if this is an *explicit* dereference.\n    /// Some types -- notably raw ptrs -- can only be dereferenced explicitly.\n    pub fn builtin_deref(&self, explicit: bool) -> Option<TypeAndMut> {\n        match self.rigid()? {\n            RigidTy::Adt(def, args) if def.is_box() => {\n                Some(TypeAndMut { ty: *args.0.first()?.ty()?, mutability: Mutability::Not })\n            }\n            RigidTy::Ref(_, ty, mutability) => {\n                Some(TypeAndMut { ty: *ty, mutability: *mutability })\n            }\n            RigidTy::RawPtr(ty, mutability) if explicit => {\n                Some(TypeAndMut { ty: *ty, mutability: *mutability })\n            }\n            _ => None,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Get the function signature for function like types (Fn, FnPtr, and Closure)\n    pub fn fn_sig(&self) -> Option<PolyFnSig> {\n        match self {\n            TyKind::RigidTy(RigidTy::FnDef(def, args)) => Some(with(|cx| cx.fn_sig(*def, args))),\n            TyKind::RigidTy(RigidTy::FnPtr(sig)) => Some(sig.clone()),\n            TyKind::RigidTy(RigidTy::Closure(_def, args)) => Some(with(|cx| cx.closure_sig(args))),\n            _ => None,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Get the discriminant type for this type.\n    pub fn discriminant_ty(&self) -> Option<Ty> {\n        self.rigid().map(|ty| with(|cx| cx.rigid_ty_discriminant_ty(ty)))\n    }\n\n    /// Deconstruct a function type if this is one.\n    pub fn fn_def(&self) -> Option<(FnDef, &GenericArgs)> {\n        if let TyKind::RigidTy(RigidTy::FnDef(def, args)) = self {\n            Some((*def, args))\n        } else {\n            None\n        }\n    }\n}\n\npub struct TypeAndMut {\n    pub ty: Ty,\n    pub mutability: Mutability,\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Vec<Option<u8>>;\n\n/// Size in bytes.\npub type Size = usize;\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Debug, Hash, Serialize)]\npub struct Prov(pub AllocId);\n\npub type Align = u64;\npub type Promoted = u32;\npub type InitMaskMaterialized = Vec<u64>;\n\n/// Stores the provenance information of pointers stored in memory.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Hash, Serialize)]\npub struct ProvenanceMap {\n    /// Provenance in this map applies from the given offset for an entire pointer-size worth of\n    /// bytes. Two entries in this map are always at least a pointer size apart.\n    pub ptrs: Vec<(Size, Prov)>,\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Hash, Serialize)]\npub struct Allocation {\n    pub bytes: Bytes,\n    pub provenance: ProvenanceMap,\n    pub align: Align,\n    pub mutability: Mutability,\n}\n\nimpl Allocation {\n    /// Get a vector of bytes for an Allocation that has been fully initialized\n    pub fn raw_bytes(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, Error> {\n        self.bytes\n            .iter()\n            .copied()\n            .collect::<Option<Vec<_>>>()\n            .ok_or_else(|| error!(\"Found uninitialized bytes: `{:?}`\", self.bytes))\n    }\n\n    /// Read a uint value from the specified range.\n    pub fn read_partial_uint(&self, range: Range<usize>) -> Result<u128, Error> {\n        if range.end - range.start > 16 {\n            return Err(error!(\"Allocation is bigger than largest integer\"));\n        }\n        if range.end > self.bytes.len() {\n            return Err(error!(\n                \"Range is out of bounds. Allocation length is `{}`, but requested range `{:?}`\",\n                self.bytes.len(),\n                range\n            ));\n        }\n        let raw = self.bytes[range]\n            .iter()\n            .copied()\n            .collect::<Option<Vec<_>>>()\n            .ok_or_else(|| error!(\"Found uninitialized bytes: `{:?}`\", self.bytes))?;\n        read_target_uint(&raw)\n    }\n\n    /// Read this allocation and try to convert it to an unassigned integer.\n    pub fn read_uint(&self) -> Result<u128, Error> {\n        if self.bytes.len() > 16 {\n            return Err(error!(\"Allocation is bigger than largest integer\"));\n        }\n        let raw = self.raw_bytes()?;\n        read_target_uint(&raw)\n    }\n\n    /// Read this allocation and try to convert it to a signed integer.\n    pub fn read_int(&self) -> Result<i128, Error> {\n        if self.bytes.len() > 16 {\n            return Err(error!(\"Allocation is bigger than largest integer\"));\n        }\n        let raw = self.raw_bytes()?;\n        read_target_int(&raw)\n    }\n\n    /// Read this allocation and try to convert it to a boolean.\n    pub fn read_bool(&self) -> Result<bool, Error> {\n        match self.read_int()? {\n            0 => Ok(false),\n            1 => Ok(true),\n            val => Err(error!(\"Unexpected value for bool: `{val}`\")),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Read this allocation as a pointer and return whether it represents a `null` pointer.\n    pub fn is_null(&self) -> Result<bool, Error> {\n        let len = self.bytes.len();\n        let ptr_len = MachineInfo::target_pointer_width().bytes();\n        if len != ptr_len {\n            return Err(error!(\"Expected width of pointer (`{ptr_len}`), but found: `{len}`\"));\n        }\n        Ok(self.read_uint()? == 0 && self.provenance.ptrs.is_empty())\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Hash, Serialize)]\npub enum ConstantKind {\n    Ty(TyConst),\n args.extend_from_slice(&gen_args.0);\n        TraitRef { def_id, args: GenericArgs(args) }\n    }\n\n    pub fn try_new(def_id: TraitDef, args: GenericArgs) -> Result<TraitRef, ()> {\n        match Analysis\n\n### Strategy\n\nThis refactoring affects the core type system of the Rust compiler across multiple crates:\n\n1. **rustc_type_ir** - Contains the generic definition and trait bounds\n2. **rustc_middle** - Contains type aliases for the tcx-specific version\n3. **rustc_public** - Contains the public FFI definition\n4. **rustc_infer** - Uses it in type inference\n5. **rustc_hir_typeck** - Uses it in fallback type inference\n6. **rustc_trait_selection** - Uses it in obligation fulfillment and error reporting\n7. **rustc_next_trait_solver** - Uses it in the next-gen trait solver\n8. **rust-analyzer** - Has its own versions of the types\n\n### Key Considerations\n\n1. **Field semantics**: The field rename from `a`/`b` to `sub_ty`/`super_ty` makes the semantics clear - `sub_ty` is the subtype and `super_ty` is the supertype in the subtype relation `sub_ty <: super_ty`.\n\n2. **Breaking changes**: This is a breaking change to the internal API. All code that pattern-matches on `SubtypePredicate` or constructs it must be updated.\n\n3. **Preservation of logic**: The refactoring is purely a renaming - no logic changes are required. All field access must be updated to use the new names.\n\n4. **Compilation order**: Changes must be made in dependency order:\n   - Start with the definitions (rustc_type_ir, rustc_public)\n   - Then type aliases and re-exports\n   - Then trait bounds and type system\n   - Finally all usage sites\n\n### Verification\n\nTo verify the refactoring is complete:\n\n1. Compile with `cargo build` in the compiler directory\n2. Check for any compilation errors mentioning `SubtypePredicate` or field names `a`/`b` in predicate context\n3. Run the test suite with `./x test`\n4. Verify no references remain with: `grep -r \"SubtypePredicate\\|\\.a\\|\\.b\" compiler/` (filtered to predicate context)\n\n### Risk Assessment\n\n- **Risk Level**: MEDIUM\n- **Impact Scope**: Wide (affects 9+ crates)\n- **Complexity**: MEDIUM (straightforward renaming but many files)\n- **Reversibility**: HIGH (simple find-replace if needed)\n\nThe refactoring is straightforward pattern-matching and field renaming with no logic changes, but the scope is large and affects core type system infrastructure.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":777,"oldLines":3,"newStart":777,"newLines":197,"lines":[" - **Reversibility**: HIGH (simple find-replace if needed)"," "," The refactoring is straightforward pattern-matching and field renaming with no logic changes, but the scope is large and affects core type system infrastructure.","+","+---","+","+# IMPLEMENTATION RESULTS","+","+## Status: COMPLETE ✓","+","+The refactoring has been successfully implemented across 24 files in the Rust compiler codebase.","+","+### Summary Statistics","+","+- **Files Modified**: 24","+- **Total Changes**: 105 insertions, 82 deletions","+- **Struct Renamed**: 1 (SubtypePredicate → SubtypeRelation)","+- **Field Names Changed**: 2 per struct (a → sub_ty, b → super_ty)","+- **References Updated**: All instances across trait bounds, type aliases, pattern matches, and field accesses","+","+### Changes Applied Successfully","+","+#### 1.
